Let me look at the code more carefully. The issue is that when `JS_NewCFunction` is called with `JS_CFUNC_generic` (which is the default for `JS_NewCFunction`), the `is_constructor` flag is not set. However, TypedArray should be marked as a constructor even though it throws an error when called.

Looking at line 57141-57142 in the original code:
```c
typed_array_base_func = JS_NewCFunction(ctx, js_typed_array_base_constructor,
                                        "TypedArray", 0);
```

The function `JS_NewCFunction` is defined in quickjs.h (line 1155-1158):
```c
static inline JSValue JS_NewCFunction(JSContext *ctx, JSCFunction *func,
                                      const char *name, int length)
{
    return JS_NewCFunction2(ctx, func, name, length, JS_CFUNC_generic, 0);
}
```

So it calls `JS_NewCFunction2` with `JS_CFUNC_generic`, which will NOT set `is_constructor = true`.

The solution is to use `JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func` instead of `JS_CFUNC_generic` for the TypedArray base constructor. This will mark it as a constructor (so it can be extended) but will still allow the constructor function to throw an error when called directly.

Let me verify this approach by checking other examples in the code:

    case JS_CFUNC_constructor:
    case JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func:
        if (!(flags & JS_CALL_FLAG_CONSTRUCTOR)) {
            if (cproto == JS_CFUNC_constructor) {
            not_a_constructor:
                ret_val = JS_ThrowTypeError(ctx, "must be called with new");
                break;
--
        /* fall thru */
    case JS_CFUNC_generic:
        ret_val = func.generic(ctx, this_obj, argc, arg_buf);
        break;
    case JS_CFUNC_constructor_magic:
    case JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func_magic:
        if (!(flags & JS_CALL_FLAG_CONSTRUCTOR)) {
            if (cproto == JS_CFUNC_constructor_magic) {
                goto not_a_constructor;
            } else {
                this_obj = JS_UNDEFINED;
--

                                        JSCFunction *func, int length,

{

Perfect! I can see that `JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func` is used in several places. Looking at lines 16323-16329 in the code (from the grep output), I can see:

```c
case JS_CFUNC_constructor:
case JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func:
    if (!(flags & JS_CALL_FLAG_CONSTRUCTOR)) {
        if (cproto == JS_CFUNC_constructor) {
        not_a_constructor:
            ret_val = JS_ThrowTypeError(ctx, "must be called with new");
            break;
```

So `JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func` will allow calling without `new` (it won't throw "must be called with new"), but it will still set `is_constructor = true`. This is exactly what we need!

However, looking at the TypedArray base constructor function:
```c
static JSValue js_typed_array_base_constructor(JSContext *ctx,
                                               JSValueConst this_val,
                                               int argc, JSValueConst *argv)
{
    return JS_ThrowTypeError(ctx, "cannot be called");
}
```

This function throws an error regardless of whether it's called with `new` or not. So using `JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func` should work perfectly - it will mark TypedArray as a constructor (allowing it to be extended) but will still throw an error when called directly (because the function body throws an error).

var TypedArray = Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array);

console.log("=== Test 1: Basic Extension ===");
try {
    class MyTypedArray extends TypedArray {}
    console.log("SUCCESS: Can extend TypedArray");
} catch (e) {
    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
}

console.log("\n=== Test 2: Cannot instantiate TypedArray directly ===");
try {
    new TypedArray();
    console.log("FAIL: Should not be able to instantiate TypedArray");
} catch (e) {
    console.log("SUCCESS:", e.message);
}

console.log("\n=== Test 3: Cannot call TypedArray as function ===");
try {
    TypedArray();
    console.log("FAIL: Should not be able to call TypedArray as function");
} catch (e) {
    console.log("SUCCESS:", e.message);
}

console.log("\n=== Test 4: Multi-level inheritance ===");
try {
    class MyTypedArray1 extends TypedArray {}
    class MyTypedArray2 extends MyTypedArray1 {}
    console.log("SUCCESS: Multi-level inheritance works");
} catch (e) {
    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
}

console.log("\n=== Test 5: Extending from TypedArray subclass ===");
try {
    class MyUint8Array extends Uint8Array {}
    var instance = new MyUint8Array(5);
    console.log("SUCCESS: Can extend Uint8Array, length =", instance.length);
} catch (e) {
    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
}

console.log("\n=== Test 6: instanceof checks ===");
try {
    class MyTypedArray extends TypedArray {}
    class MyUint8Array extends Uint8Array {}
    var arr = new MyUint8Array(5);
    console.log("arr instanceof MyUint8Array:", arr instanceof MyUint8Array);
    console.log("arr instanceof Uint8Array:", arr instanceof Uint8Array);
    console.log("arr instanceof TypedArray:", arr instanceof TypedArray);
    console.log("SUCCESS: instanceof checks work");
} catch (e) {
    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
}

console.log("\n=== Test 7: All TypedArray constructors share same base ===");
try {
    var bases = [
        Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array),
        Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint16Array),
        Object.getPrototypeOf(Int8Array),
        Object.getPrototypeOf(Int16Array),
        Object.getPrototypeOf(Float32Array),
        Object.getPrototypeOf(Float64Array)
    ];
    var allSame = bases.every(b => b === TypedArray);
    console.log("All TypedArray constructors share same base:", allSame);
} catch (e) {
    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
}

console.log("\n=== Test 8: TypedArray.prototype ===");
try {
    console.log("TypedArray.prototype:", TypedArray.prototype);
    console.log("Uint8Array.prototype.__proto__ === TypedArray.prototype:", 
                Uint8Array.prototype.__proto__ === TypedArray.prototype);
} catch (e) {
    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
}

try {
    class MyTypedArray extends TypedArray {
        constructor() {
            // This won'"'"'t work because TypedArray constructor throws
            // but let'"'"'s test the class definition itself
        }
    }
    console.log("SUCCESS: Can define constructor in extended class");
} catch (e) {
    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
}

try {

    eval(code);
    console.log("SUCCESS: TypedArray can be used in extends clause");
} catch (e) {
    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
}

/*---
includes: [sm/non262.js, sm/non262-shell.js, sm/non262-TypedArray-shell.js]

  pending
esid: pending

/*
 * Any copyright is dedicated to the Public Domain.
 * http://creativecommons.org/publicdomain/zero/1.0/
 */

var gTestfile = 'prototype-constructor-identity.js';
//-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
var BUGNUMBER = 896116;
var summary =
  "Typed array prototypes/constructors should be largely empty, inheriting "
  "most functionality from %TypedArray% and %TypedArray%.prototype";

print(BUGNUMBER + ": " + summary);

/**************
 * BEGIN TEST *
 **************/

var TypedArray = Object.getPrototypeOf(Int8Array);

assert.sameValue(TypedArray !== Function.prototype, true,
         "%TypedArray% should be in constructors' [[Prototype]] chains");
assert.sameValue(Object.getPrototypeOf(TypedArray), Function.prototype,
         "%TypedArray%.prototype should inherit from Function.prototype");

assert.sameValue(TypedArray.prototype.constructor, TypedArray,
         "bad %TypedArray%.prototype.constructor");

// Check a few different functions we implement are here, as a sanity check.
var typedArrayProps = Object.getOwnPropertyNames(TypedArray.prototype);
assert.sameValue(typedArrayProps.indexOf("copyWithin") >= 0, true);
assert.sameValue(typedArrayProps.indexOf("subarray") >= 0, true);
assert.sameValue(typedArrayProps.indexOf("set") >= 0, true);

anyTypedArrayConstructors.forEach(function(ctor) {
  assert.sameValue(Object.getPrototypeOf(ctor), TypedArray);

  var proto = ctor.prototype;

  // Inherited functions aren't present.
  var props = Object.getOwnPropertyNames(proto).sort();
  assert.sameValue(props[0], "BYTES_PER_ELEMENT");
  assert.sameValue(props[1], "constructor");
  if (ctor === Uint8Array) {
    assert.sameValue(props.length, 6);
  } else {
    assert.sameValue(props.length, 2);
  }

  // The inheritance chain should be set up properly.
  assert.sameValue(Object.getPrototypeOf(proto), TypedArray.prototype,
           "prototype should inherit from %TypedArray%.prototype");
});

/******************************************************************************/

print("Tests complete");

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_typedarray_complete.js --file_text '/*
 * Test: TypedArray can be extended (but not instantiated)
 * 
 * According to ECMAScript specification, the TypedArray constructor (which is
 * Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array)) should be extendable but not directly
 * instantiable since it'"'"'s abstract.
 * 
 * This test verifies that:
 * 1. TypedArray can be used in an extends clause
 * 2. TypedArray cannot be called directly (with or without new)
 * 3. Classes extending TypedArray work correctly
 */

// Get the TypedArray constructor
var TypedArray = Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array);

console.log("Test 1: TypedArray can be extended");
try {
    class MyTypedArray extends TypedArray {}
    console.log("✓ PASS: Can extend TypedArray");
} catch (e) {
    console.log("✗ FAIL: Cannot extend TypedArray -", e.message);
    throw e;
}

console.log("\nTest 2: TypedArray cannot be instantiated with new");
try {
    new TypedArray();
    console.log("✗ FAIL: TypedArray should not be instantiable");
    throw new Error("TypedArray should throw when instantiated");
} catch (e) {
    if (e.message.includes("cannot be called")) {
        console.log("✓ PASS: TypedArray throws when instantiated -", e.message);
    } else {
        throw e;
    }
}

console.log("\nTest 3: TypedArray cannot be called as function");
try {
    TypedArray();
    console.log("✗ FAIL: TypedArray should not be callable");
    throw new Error("TypedArray should throw when called");
} catch (e) {
    if (e.message.includes("cannot be called")) {
        console.log("✓ PASS: TypedArray throws when called -", e.message);
    } else {
        throw e;
    }
}

console.log("\nTest 4: All typed array constructors have same parent");
var constructors = [
    Uint8Array, Uint16Array, Uint32Array,
    Int8Array, Int16Array, Int32Array,
    Float32Array, Float64Array,
    Uint8ClampedArray
];

var allMatch = constructors.every(function(ctor) {
    return Object.getPrototypeOf(ctor) === TypedArray;
});

if (allMatch) {
    console.log("✓ PASS: All typed array constructors have TypedArray as parent");
} else {
    console.log("✗ FAIL: Not all typed array constructors have TypedArray as parent");
    throw new Error("TypedArray inheritance broken");
}

console.log("\nTest 5: TypedArray has correct prototype chain");
var proto = Uint8Array.prototype.__proto__;
if (proto === TypedArray.prototype) {
    console.log("✓ PASS: Uint8Array.prototype.__proto__ === TypedArray.prototype");
} else {
    console.log("✗ FAIL: Incorrect prototype chain");
    throw new Error("Prototype chain broken");
}

console.log("\n✓✓✓ All tests passed! ✓✓✓");
'

Let me now document the change with a summary:\n\n## Summary\n\nThe issue was that TypedArray (which is `Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array)`) could not be used in an `extends` clause, even though according to the ECMAScript specification, it should be extendable (but not directly instantiable since it\'s abstract).\n\n### Root Cause\nThe TypedArray base constructor was created using `JS_NewCFunction()`, which uses the `JS_CFUNC_generic` function type. This function type does not set the `is_constructor` flag on the function object. When JavaScript tries to extend a class, it checks if the parent class has the constructor flag set via `JS_IsConstructor()`. If not, it throws "TypeError: parent class must be constructor".\n\n### Solution\nChanged the TypedArray base constructor to be created with `JS_NewCFunction2()` using the `JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func` function type instead of `JS_CFUNC_generic`. This sets the `is_constructor` flag to true, allowing TypedArray to be extended, while still preserving its abstract nature (it throws "cannot be called" when instantiated).\n\n### Code Change\nIn `/testbed/quickjs.c` at line 57141-57142:\n\n**Before:**\n```c\ntyped_array_base_func = JS_NewCFunction(ctx, js_typed_array_base_constructor,\n                                        "TypedArray", 0);\n```\n\n**After:**\n```c\ntyped_array_base_func = JS_NewCFunction2(ctx, js_typed_array_base_constructor,\n                                         "TypedArray", 0, JS_CFUNC_constructor_or_func, 0);\n```\n\n### Behavior\n- ✅ TypedArray can now be extended: `class MyClass extends TypedArray {}`\n- ✅ TypedArray remains abstract: `new TypedArray()` throws "cannot be called"\n- ✅ TypedArray cannot be called as function: `TypedArray()` throws "cannot be called"\n- ✅ All existing tests pass\n- ✅ Prototype chains remain intact\n\nThe fix is minimal, changes only one line effectively, and maintains backward compatibility while enabling the correct ECMAScript behavior for extending TypedArray.', refusal=None, role='assistant', annotations=None, audio=None, function_call=None, tool_calls=None))], created=1766665488, model='claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929', object='chat.completion', service_tier=None, system_fingerprint=None, usage=CompletionUsage(completion_tokens=539, prompt_tokens=37307, total_tokens=37846, completion_tokens_details=CompletionTokensDetails(accepted_prediction_tokens=None, audio_tokens=0, reasoning_tokens=0, rejected_prediction_tokens=None, text_tokens=0), prompt_tokens_details=PromptTokensDetails(audio_tokens=0, cached_tokens=0, text_tokens=0, image_tokens=0), input_tokens=0, output_tokens=0, input_tokens_details=None, claude_cache_creation_5_m_tokens=0, claude_cache_creation_1_h_tokens=0))

+// Test edge cases for TypedArray extending
+var TypedArray = Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array);
+
+console.log("=== Test 1: Basic Extension ===");
+try {
+    class MyTypedArray extends TypedArray {}
+    console.log("SUCCESS: Can extend TypedArray");
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
+}
+
+console.log("\n=== Test 2: Cannot instantiate TypedArray directly ===");
+try {
+    new TypedArray();
+    console.log("FAIL: Should not be able to instantiate TypedArray");
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("SUCCESS:", e.message);
+}
+
+console.log("\n=== Test 3: Cannot call TypedArray as function ===");
+try {
+    TypedArray();
+    console.log("FAIL: Should not be able to call TypedArray as function");
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("SUCCESS:", e.message);
+}
+
+console.log("\n=== Test 4: Multi-level inheritance ===");
+try {
+    class MyTypedArray1 extends TypedArray {}
+    class MyTypedArray2 extends MyTypedArray1 {}
+    console.log("SUCCESS: Multi-level inheritance works");
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
+}
+
+console.log("\n=== Test 5: Extending from TypedArray subclass ===");
+try {
+    class MyUint8Array extends Uint8Array {}
+    var instance = new MyUint8Array(5);
+    console.log("SUCCESS: Can extend Uint8Array, length =", instance.length);
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
+}
+
+console.log("\n=== Test 6: instanceof checks ===");
+try {
+    class MyTypedArray extends TypedArray {}
+    class MyUint8Array extends Uint8Array {}
+    var arr = new MyUint8Array(5);
+    console.log("arr instanceof MyUint8Array:", arr instanceof MyUint8Array);
+    console.log("arr instanceof Uint8Array:", arr instanceof Uint8Array);
+    console.log("arr instanceof TypedArray:", arr instanceof TypedArray);
+    console.log("SUCCESS: instanceof checks work");
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
+}
+
+console.log("\n=== Test 7: All TypedArray constructors share same base ===");
+try {
+    var bases = [
+        Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array),
+        Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint16Array),
+        Object.getPrototypeOf(Int8Array),
+        Object.getPrototypeOf(Int16Array),
+        Object.getPrototypeOf(Float32Array),
+        Object.getPrototypeOf(Float64Array)
+    ];
+    var allSame = bases.every(b => b === TypedArray);
+    console.log("All TypedArray constructors share same base:", allSame);
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);
+}
+
+console.log("\n=== Test 8: TypedArray.prototype ===");
+try {
+    console.log("TypedArray.prototype:", TypedArray.prototype);
+    console.log("Uint8Array.prototype.__proto__ === TypedArray.prototype:", 
+                Uint8Array.prototype.__proto__ === TypedArray.prototype);

+    console.log("FAIL:", e.message);

@@ -0,0 +1,80 @@
+/*
+ * Test: TypedArray can be extended (but not instantiated)
+ * 
+ * According to ECMAScript specification, the TypedArray constructor (which is
+ * Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array)) should be extendable but not directly
+ * instantiable since it's abstract.
+ * 
+ * This test verifies that:
+ * 1. TypedArray can be used in an extends clause
+ * 2. TypedArray cannot be called directly (with or without new)
+ * 3. Classes extending TypedArray work correctly
+ */
+
+// Get the TypedArray constructor
+var TypedArray = Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array);
+
+console.log("Test 1: TypedArray can be extended");
+try {
+    class MyTypedArray extends TypedArray {}
+    console.log("✓ PASS: Can extend TypedArray");
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("✗ FAIL: Cannot extend TypedArray -", e.message);
+    throw e;
+}
+
+console.log("\nTest 2: TypedArray cannot be instantiated with new");
+try {
+    new TypedArray();
+    console.log("✗ FAIL: TypedArray should not be instantiable");
+    throw new Error("TypedArray should throw when instantiated");
+} catch (e) {
+    if (e.message.includes("cannot be called")) {
+        console.log("✓ PASS: TypedArray throws when instantiated -", e.message);
+    } else {
+        throw e;
+    }
+}
+
+console.log("\nTest 3: TypedArray cannot be called as function");
+try {
+    TypedArray();
+    console.log("✗ FAIL: TypedArray should not be callable");
+    throw new Error("TypedArray should throw when called");
+} catch (e) {
+    if (e.message.includes("cannot be called")) {
+        console.log("✓ PASS: TypedArray throws when called -", e.message);
+    } else {
+        throw e;
+    }
+}
+
+console.log("\nTest 4: All typed array constructors have same parent");
+var constructors = [
+    Uint8Array, Uint16Array, Uint32Array,
+    Int8Array, Int16Array, Int32Array,
+    Float32Array, Float64Array,
+    Uint8ClampedArray
+];
+
+var allMatch = constructors.every(function(ctor) {
+    return Object.getPrototypeOf(ctor) === TypedArray;
+});
+
+if (allMatch) {
+    console.log("✓ PASS: All typed array constructors have TypedArray as parent");
+} else {
+    console.log("✗ FAIL: Not all typed array constructors have TypedArray as parent");
+    throw new Error("TypedArray inheritance broken");
+}
+
+console.log("\nTest 5: TypedArray has correct prototype chain");
+var proto = Uint8Array.prototype.__proto__;
+if (proto === TypedArray.prototype) {
+    console.log("✓ PASS: Uint8Array.prototype.__proto__ === TypedArray.prototype");
+} else {
+    console.log("✗ FAIL: Incorrect prototype chain");
+    throw new Error("Prototype chain broken");
+}
+
+console.log("\n✓✓✓ All tests passed! ✓✓✓");

+// Test extending TypedArray
+var TypedArray = Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array);
+
+console.log("TypedArray:", TypedArray);
+console.log("TypedArray name:", TypedArray.name);
+
+// This should work according to the PR
+try {
+    var MyClass = class extends TypedArray {};
+    console.log("SUCCESS: Can extend TypedArray");
+    console.log("MyClass:", MyClass);
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("ERROR: Cannot extend TypedArray -", e.message);

+

+try {
+    new TypedArray();
+    console.log("ERROR: TypedArray should not be instantiable");
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("SUCCESS: TypedArray is not instantiable -", e.message);

+try {
+    function MyFunc() {}
+    MyFunc.prototype = Object.create(TypedArray.prototype);
+    MyFunc.prototype.constructor = MyFunc;
+    Object.setPrototypeOf(MyFunc, TypedArray);
+    console.log("SUCCESS: Can set TypedArray as prototype");
+} catch (e) {
+    console.log("ERROR: Cannot set TypedArray as prototype -", e.message);
+}
